**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is May, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

# DAILY BRIEFING: MAY 2025

## 1: TRUMP ADMINISTRATION EXECUTIVE ACTIONS

### 1.1: Federal Funding Decisions and Budget Cuts

The Trump administration has enacted significant funding restrictions targeting research institutions and cultural programs. Harvard University faces multiple punitive measures, including an $8 billion pause on grant funding [1] and being barred from new federal research funding [2] until meeting unspecified presidential demands [3]. Beyond higher education, the National Institutes of Health has laid off hundreds of staff, including at cancer research institutes [4], while the National Endowment for the Arts is sending grant terminations as Trump's budget proposes shuttering the agency [5]. The administration has also cut the 'Safe to Sleep' infant safety team [6].

His order to reopen Alcatraz prison [5] has drawn mixed public reactions from calling Trump "a moron" to saying the "idea seems good" [6], with critics alleging he is "stealing his policy ideas from TV" [7].

## 2: IMMIGRATION ENFORCEMENT AND BORDER SECURITY

### 2.1: Detention Conditions and Deportation Operations

Immigration enforcement has intensified with concerning humanitarian implications. Seven migrants have died in Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) custody during Trump's first 100 days [1], raising significant questions about detention conditions. The administration has reportedly deported individuals previously protected by legal settlements [2] while negotiating with Rwanda to accept deportees [3], which Rwandan officials have confirmed [4]. 

A federal judge has ordered the Trump administration to admit approximately 12,000 refugees [5], presenting a significant judicial challenge to refugee admission restrictions. Border security measures have intensified, with worsening cross-border travel from British Columbia to Washington state [6] and U.S. Border Agents requesting help photographing everyone entering the country by car [7].

## 3: LEGAL CHALLENGES AND JUDICIAL OVERSIGHT

### 3.1: Justice Department Positions and Court Interventions

The Trump Justice Department has taken notable positions on reproductive rights cases, urging a judge to dismiss states' lawsuits over access to the abortion pill mifepristone [1] while committing to defend Biden-era abortion pill rules in a Texas case [2]. These positions demonstrate policy continuity on specific issues despite broader differences between the administrations.

Judicial intervention has emerged in electoral processes, with a federal judge ordering North Carolina to certify Democrat Allison Riggs as winner in a state Supreme Court election [3]. In Michigan, the Attorney General has dropped all charges against seven pro-Palestinian protesters [4], reflecting tensions between protest activities and law enforcement in politically sensitive contexts.

## 4: DOMESTIC POLITICS AND GOVERNANCE

### 4.1: Congressional Activities and Political Opposition

Former Vice President Mike Pence has publicly diverged from President Trump on tariffs, Russia relations, and potential January 6 pardons [1], specifically rebuking Trump over tariffs and "wavering" support for Ukraine [2]. Representative Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez has declined to seek the top Democratic position on the House Oversight Committee [3], citing deference to seniority.

Opposition to the administration manifests through multiple channels. Former Palantir employees have condemned the company's work with the Trump administration [4], while Senator Bernie Sanders stated that "resisting Trump is 'not good enough'" [5]. Publications have examined how "Republicans in Congress enable Trump's tyranny" [6], while a former official claims Trump is trying to silence critics [7]. 

At the state level, Georgia Governor Brian Kemp has declined to run for Senate despite private lobbying [8], while a Maryland town that supported Trump's cost-cutting pledge has reportedly become a target of those same policies [9].

## 5: INTERNATIONAL RELATIONS AND NATIONAL SECURITY

### 5.1: Defense Policy and Global Conflicts

Defense Secretary Hegseth has initiated significant structural changes, directing a 20% reduction in top military leadership positions [1] as part of slashing the military's senior-most ranks [2]. In a move that reportedly surprised the White House, Hegseth issued an order to cancel Ukraine weapons deliveries [3], indicating potential policy discord within the administration. 

The Israel-Palestine conflict continues to intensify. Israel has approved a plan to capture all of Gaza and called up tens of thousands of reserve troops [4], while U.S. public opinion has shifted, with reports that "Americans used to be steadfast in their support for Israel. Those days are gone" [5]. An Israeli news investigation claims the Biden administration did not try to end what the source characterizes as genocide in Gaza [6].

In U.S.-Russia relations, Polish President Andrzej Duda has called on Trump to pressure Russia with "economic instruments" [7], while former Vice President Pence emphasized that "Putin doesn't want peace, he wants Ukraine" while rebuking Trump's stance on Russia [8].
